For further discussion, see <i><a href="/wiki/Exergy" title="Exergy">Exergy</a></i>.
</p><p>Statistical mechanics demonstrates that entropy is governed by probability, thus allowing for a decrease in disorder even in an isolated system. Although this is possible, such an event has a small probability of occurring, making it unlikely.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The applicability of a second law of thermodynamics is limited to systems in or sufficiently near <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_equilibrium" title="Thermodynamic equilibrium">equilibrium state</a>, so that they have defined entropy.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Some inhomogeneous systems out of thermodynamic equilibrium still satisfy the hypothesis of <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_equilibrium#local_and_global_equilibrium" title="Thermodynamic equilibrium">local thermodynamic equilibrium</a>, so that entropy density is locally defined as an intensive quantity. For such systems, there may apply a principle of maximum time rate of entropy production.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> It states that such a system may evolve to a steady state that maximizes its time rate of entropy production. This does not mean that such a system is necessarily always in a condition of maximum time rate of entropy production; it means that it may evolve to such a steady state.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_fundamental_thermodynamic_relation">The fundamental thermodynamic relation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The fundamental thermodynamic relation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_thermodynamic_relation" title="Fundamental thermodynamic relation">Fundamental thermodynamic relation</a></div>
<p>The entropy of a system depends on its internal energy and its external parameters, such as its volume. In the thermodynamic limit, this fact leads to an equation relating the change in the internal energy <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle U}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>U</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle U}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/458a728f53b9a0274f059cd695e067c430956025" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.783ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="U"/></span> to changes in the entropy and the external parameters. This relation is known as the <i>fundamental thermodynamic relation</i>. If external pressure <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle p}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>p</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="p"/></span> bears on the volume <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle V}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>V</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle V}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/af0f6064540e84211d0ffe4dac72098adfa52845" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.787ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="V"/></span> as the only external parameter, this relation is:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle dU=T\,dS-p\,dV}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>U</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>T</mi>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mi>p</mi>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>V</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle dU=T\,dS-p\,dV}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a5b2b11ff8b0c50701f96617c129001a7c7b0158" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:18.235ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle dU=T\,dS-p\,dV}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Since both internal energy and entropy are monotonic functions of temperature <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle T}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>T</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec7200acd984a1d3a3d7dc455e262fbe54f7f6e0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.636ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="T"/></span>, implying that the internal energy is fixed when one specifies the entropy and the volume, this relation is valid even if the change from one state of thermal equilibrium to another with infinitesimally larger entropy and volume happens in a non-quasistatic way (so during this change the system may be very far out of thermal equilibrium and then the whole-system entropy, pressure, and temperature may not exist).
</p><p>The fundamental thermodynamic relation implies many thermodynamic identities that are valid in general, independent of the microscopic details of the system. Important examples are the <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_relations" title="Maxwell relations">Maxwell relations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Relations_between_heat_capacities" title="Relations between heat capacities">relations between heat capacities</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entropy_in_chemical_thermodynamics">Entropy in chemical thermodynamics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Entropy in chemical thermodynamics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Thermodynamic entropy is central in <a href="/wiki/Chemical_thermodynamics" title="Chemical thermodynamics">chemical thermodynamics</a>, enabling changes to be quantified and the outcome of reactions predicted. The <a href="/wiki/Second_law_of_thermodynamics" title="Second law of thermodynamics">second law of thermodynamics</a> states that entropy in an <a href="/wiki/Isolated_system" title="Isolated system">isolated system</a> – the combination of a subsystem under study and its surroundings – increases during all spontaneous chemical and physical processes. The Clausius equation of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \delta q_{\text{rev}}/T=\Delta S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03B4;<!-- δ --></mi>
        <msub>
          <mi>q</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mtext>rev</mtext>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo>/</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mi>T</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x0394;<!-- Δ --></mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \delta q_{\text{rev}}/T=\Delta S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b9851fa43f6438b7f103976267dd73b68a283601" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.893ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \delta q_{\text{rev}}/T=\Delta S}"/></span> introduces the measurement of entropy change, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x0394;<!-- Δ --></mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \Delta S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/15a2efec755f08f95da4e8d1f7f2682861fb59be" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.435ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\Delta S"/></span>. Entropy change describes the direction and quantifies the magnitude of simple changes such as heat transfer between systems – always from hotter to cooler spontaneously.
</p><p>The thermodynamic entropy therefore has the dimension of energy divided by temperature, and the unit <a href="/wiki/Joule" title="Joule">joule</a> per <a href="/wiki/Kelvin" title="Kelvin">kelvin</a> (J/K) in the International System of Units (SI).
</p><p>Thermodynamic entropy is an <a href="/wiki/Intensive_and_extensive_properties" title="Intensive and extensive properties">extensive</a> property, meaning that it scales with the size or extent of a system. In many processes it is useful to specify the entropy as an <a href="/wiki/Intensive_and_extensive_properties" title="Intensive and extensive properties">intensive property</a> independent of the size, as a specific entropy characteristic of the type of system studied. Specific entropy may be expressed relative to a unit of mass, typically the kilogram (unit: J⋅kg<sup>−1</sup>⋅K<sup>−1</sup>). Alternatively, in chemistry, it is also referred to one <a href="/wiki/Mole_(unit)" title="Mole (unit)">mole</a> of substance, in which case it is called the <i>molar entropy</i> with a unit of J⋅mol<sup>−1</sup>⋅K<sup>−1</sup>.
</p><p>Thus, when one mole of substance at about <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="5000000000000000000♠"></span>0&#160;K</span> is warmed by its surroundings to <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7002298000000000000♠"></span>298&#160;K</span>, the sum of the incremental values of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle q_{\text{rev}}/T}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>q</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mtext>rev</mtext>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo>/</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mi>T</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\textstyle q_{\text{rev}}/T}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/eb51a4de03b105ddb5d18f62d2a8f35e29d8b3b9" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.311ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\textstyle q_{\text{rev}}/T}"/></span> constitute each element's or compound's standard molar entropy, an indicator of the amount of energy stored by a substance at <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7002298000000000000♠"></span>298&#160;K</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-ctms_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ctms-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jungermann_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jungermann-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Entropy change also measures the mixing of substances as a summation of their relative quantities in the final mixture.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Entropy is equally essential in predicting the extent and direction of complex chemical reactions. For such applications, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \Delta S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/15a2efec755f08f95da4e8d1f7f2682861fb59be" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.435ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\Delta S"/></span> must be incorporated in an expression that includes both the system and its surroundings, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta S_{\text{universe}}=\Delta S_{\text{surroundings}}+\Delta S_{\text{system}}}">

<h3><span id="World.27s_technological_capacity_to_store_and_communicate_entropic_information"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World's_technological_capacity_to_store_and_communicate_entropic_information">World's technological capacity to store and communicate entropic information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: World&#039;s technological capacity to store and communicate entropic information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 2011 study in <a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science (journal)</a> estimated the world's technological capacity to store and communicate optimally compressed information normalized on the most effective compression algorithms available in the year 2007, therefore estimating the entropy of the technologically available sources.<sup id="cite_ref-HilbertLopez2011_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HilbertLopez2011-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The author's estimate that human kind's technological capacity to store information grew from 2.6 (entropically compressed) <a href="/wiki/Exabytes" class="mw-redirect" title="Exabytes">exabytes</a> in 1986 to 295 (entropically compressed) <a href="/wiki/Exabytes" class="mw-redirect" title="Exabytes">exabytes</a> in 2007. The world's technological capacity to receive information through one-way broadcast networks was 432 <a href="/wiki/Exabytes" class="mw-redirect" title="Exabytes">exabytes</a> of (entropically compressed) information in 1986, to 1.9 <a href="/wiki/Zettabytes" class="mw-redirect" title="Zettabytes">zettabytes</a> in 2007. The world's effective capacity to exchange information through two-way telecommunication networks was 281 <a href="/wiki/Petabytes" class="mw-redirect" title="Petabytes">petabytes</a> of (entropically compressed) information in 1986, to 65 (entropically compressed) <a href="/wiki/Exabytes" class="mw-redirect" title="Exabytes">exabytes</a> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-HilbertLopez2011_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HilbertLopez2011-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entropy_balance_equation_for_open_systems">Entropy balance equation for open systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Entropy balance equation for open systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_law_open_system.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/First_law_open_system.svg/310px-First_law_open_system.svg.png" decoding="async" width="310" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/First_law_open_system.svg/465px-First_law_open_system.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/First_law_open_system.svg/620px-First_law_open_system.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="374" data-file-height="257" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_law_open_system.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>During <a href="/wiki/Steady-state_(chemical_engineering)" class="mw-redirect" title="Steady-state (chemical engineering)">steady-state</a> continuous operation, an entropy balance applied to an open system accounts for system entropy changes related to heat flow and mass flow across the system boundary.</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">chemical engineering</a>, the principles of thermodynamics are commonly applied to "<a href="/wiki/Open_system_(systems_theory)" title="Open system (systems theory)">open systems</a>", i.e. those in which heat, <a href="/wiki/Work_(thermodynamics)" title="Work (thermodynamics)">work</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mass" title="Mass">mass</a> flow across the system boundary. Flows of both heat (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\dot {Q}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

              <mi>Q</mi>
              <mo>&#x02D9;<!-- ˙ --></mo>
            </mover>

      </mstyle>
    </mrow>

    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>P</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>V</mi>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo>/</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>t</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P(dV/dt)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/799823b1305643a01bf2e891dc90e575af40c532" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.776ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle P(dV/dt)}"/></span> (pressure-volume work), across the system boundaries, in general cause changes in the entropy of the system. Transfer as heat entails entropy transfer <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\dot {Q}}/T}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mover>
              <mi>Q</mi>
              <mo>&#x02D9;<!-- ˙ --></mo>
            </mover>
          </mrow>
        </mrow>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo>/</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mi>T</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\dot {Q}}/T}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/724e05a0d5e2f0378879ec58264544bb71dbe09c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.637ex; height:3.343ex;" alt="{\dot {Q}}/T"/></span>, where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle T}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>T</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec7200acd984a1d3a3d7dc455e262fbe54f7f6e0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.636ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="T"/></span> is the absolute <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_temperature" title="Thermodynamic temperature">thermodynamic temperature</a> of the system at the point of the heat flow. If there are mass flows across the system boundaries, they also influence the total entropy of the system. This account, in terms of heat and work, is valid only for cases in which the work and heat transfers are by paths physically distinct from the paths of entry and exit of matter from the system.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To derive a generalized entropy balanced equation, we start with the general balance equation for the change in any <a href="/wiki/Extensive_quantity" class="mw-redirect" title="Extensive quantity">extensive quantity</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \theta }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03B8;<!-- θ --></mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \theta }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e5ab2664b422d53eb0c7df3b87e1360d75ad9af" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\theta "/></span> in a <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_system" title="Thermodynamic system">thermodynamic system</a>, a quantity that may be either conserved, such as energy, or non-conserved, such as entropy. The basic generic balance expression states that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle d\theta /dt}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>&#x03B8;<!-- θ --></mi>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo>/</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>t</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle d\theta /dt}</annotation>
  </semantics>

  <semantics>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e5ab2664b422d53eb0c7df3b87e1360d75ad9af" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\theta "/></span> enters the system at the boundaries, minus the rate at which <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \theta }">

  <semantics>

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e5ab2664b422d53eb0c7df3b87e1360d75ad9af" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\theta "/></span> is generated within the system. For an open thermodynamic system in which heat and work are transferred by paths separate from the paths for transfer of matter, using this generic balance equation, with respect to the rate of change with time <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle t}">

<p>If there are multiple heat flows, the term <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\dot {Q}}/T}">

      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mover>
                <mi>Q</mi>
                <mo>&#x02D9;<!-- ˙ --></mo>
              </mover>
            </mrow>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>j</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\dot {Q}}_{j}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3297f80aa6199c9123c2650a250fea4e61c2c194" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.171ex; width:2.748ex; height:3.676ex;" alt="{\dot {Q}}_{j}"/></span> is the heat flow and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle T_{j}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>T</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>j</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T_{j}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/27cdb9041c8aa769beb9153a48f41002297faacc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.267ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="T_{j}"/></span> is the temperature at the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle j}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>j</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle j}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2f461e54f5c093e92a55547b9764291390f0b5d0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.027ex; width:0.985ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="j"/></span>th heat flow port into the system.
</p><p>Note that the nomenclature "entropy balance" is misleading and often deemed inappropriate because entropy is not a conserved quantity. In other words, the term <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\dot {S}}_{\text{gen}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mover>
                <mi>S</mi>
                <mo>&#x02D9;<!-- ˙ --></mo>
              </mover>
            </mrow>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mtext>gen</mtext>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\dot {S}}_{\text{gen}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5b2a1ba7ce131c02e4157de6d23cacc651c7a334" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:4.271ex; height:3.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\dot {S}}_{\text{gen}}}"/></span> is never a known quantity but always a derived one based on the expression above. Therefore, the open system version of the second law is more appropriately described as the "entropy generation equation" since it specifies that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\dot {S}}_{\text{gen}}\geq 0}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mover>
                <mi>S</mi>
                <mo>&#x02D9;<!-- ˙ --></mo>
              </mover>
            </mrow>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mtext>gen</mtext>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2265;<!-- ≥ --></mo>
        <mn>0</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\dot {S}}_{\text{gen}}\geq 0}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/26a116bc55daf256bd0bf42bbec45eaaab8085ac" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:8.532ex; height:3.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\dot {S}}_{\text{gen}}\geq 0}"/></span>, with zero for reversible processes or greater than zero for irreversible ones.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Entropy_change_formulas_for_simple_processes">Entropy change formulas for simple processes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Entropy change formulas for simple processes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>For certain simple transformations in systems of constant composition, the entropy changes are given by simple formulas.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Isothermal_expansion_or_compression_of_an_ideal_gas">Isothermal expansion or compression of an ideal gas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Isothermal expansion or compression of an ideal gas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For the expansion (or compression) of an <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas" title="Ideal gas">ideal gas</a> from an initial volume <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle V_{0}}">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/af0f6064540e84211d0ffe4dac72098adfa52845" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.787ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="V"/></span> and pressure <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P}">

</p>

<p>Here <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle n}">

These equations also apply for expansion into a finite vacuum or a <a href="/wiki/Throttling_process_(thermodynamics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Throttling process (thermodynamics)">throttling process</a>, where the temperature, internal energy and enthalpy for an ideal gas remain constant.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooling_and_heating">Cooling and heating</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cooling and heating">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For pure heating or cooling of any system (gas, liquid or solid) at constant pressure from an initial temperature <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle T_{0}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>T</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>0</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T_{0}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/55b9e7d7b96196b5a6a26f4349caa3ac82fd67e3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.412ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="T_{0}"/></span> to a final temperature <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle T}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>T</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec7200acd984a1d3a3d7dc455e262fbe54f7f6e0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.636ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="T"/></span>, the entropy change is
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{P}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}}.}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x0394;<!-- Δ --></mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>n</mi>
        <msub>
          <mi>C</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>P</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>ln</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mi>T</mi>
            <msub>
              <mi>T</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>0</mn>
              </mrow>
            </msub>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{P}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}}.}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/66c69e2c87c00ead35b540e39af1d45cfcdea60b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:17.665ex; height:5.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{P}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}}.}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>provided that the constant-pressure molar <a href="/wiki/Heat_capacity" title="Heat capacity">heat capacity</a> (or specific heat) <i>C</i><sub><i>P</i></sub> is constant and that no <a href="/wiki/Phase_transition" title="Phase transition">phase transition</a> occurs in this temperature interval.
</p><p>Similarly at constant volume, the entropy change is
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{v}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}},}">

      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>n</mi>
        <msub>
          <mi>C</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>v</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>ln</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mi>T</mi>
            <msub>
              <mi>T</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>0</mn>
              </mrow>
            </msub>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{v}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}},}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3c7fb198511fc79719c97bb94078743c372423e8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:17.228ex; height:5.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{v}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}},}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where the constant-volume molar heat capacity <i>C</i><sub>v</sub> is constant and there is no phase change.
</p><p>At low temperatures near absolute zero, <a href="/wiki/Debye_T3_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Debye T3 law">heat capacities of solids quickly drop off to near zero</a>, so the assumption of constant heat capacity does not apply.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since entropy is a <a href="/wiki/Functions_of_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Functions of state">state function</a>, the entropy change of any process in which temperature and volume both vary is the same as for a path divided into two steps – heating at constant volume and expansion at constant temperature. For an ideal gas, the total entropy change is<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{v}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}}+nR\ln {\frac {V}{V_{0}}}.}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x0394;<!-- Δ --></mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>n</mi>
        <msub>
          <mi>C</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>v</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>ln</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mi>T</mi>
            <msub>
              <mi>T</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>0</mn>
              </mrow>
            </msub>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>+</mo>
        <mi>n</mi>
        <mi>R</mi>
        <mi>ln</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mi>V</mi>
            <msub>
              <mi>V</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>0</mn>
              </mrow>
            </msub>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{v}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}}+nR\ln {\frac {V}{V_{0}}}.}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2306c78613f0ef900d643049753f9ed9b57403c9" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:29.186ex; height:5.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{v}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}}+nR\ln {\frac {V}{V_{0}}}.}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Similarly if the temperature and pressure of an ideal gas both vary,
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta S=nC_{P}\ln {\frac {T}{T_{0}}}-nR\ln {\frac {P}{P_{0}}}.}">
  <semantics>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_transitions">Phase transitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Phase transitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Reversible <a href="/wiki/Phase_transition" title="Phase transition">phase transitions</a> occur at constant temperature and pressure. The reversible heat is the enthalpy change for the transition, and the entropy change is the enthalpy change divided by the thermodynamic temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> For fusion (<a href="/wiki/Melting" title="Melting">melting</a>) of a solid to a liquid at the melting point <i>T</i><sub>m</sub>, the <a href="/wiki/Entropy_of_fusion" title="Entropy of fusion">entropy of fusion</a> is
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Delta S_{\text{fus}}={\frac {\Delta H_{\text{fus}}}{T_{\text{m}}}}.}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

          </mrow>
        </msub>

                  <mtext>fus</mtext>
                </mrow>

            </mrow>
            <msub>

              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mtext>m</mtext>
              </mrow>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/53db9b886a2366c975fde12d9b83b90dde1b5c59" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:16.404ex; height:5.676ex;" alt="\Delta S_{\text{fus}}={\frac {\Delta H_{\text{fus}}}{T_{\text{m}}}}."/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Similarly, for <a href="/wiki/Vaporization" title="Vaporization">vaporization</a> of a liquid to a gas at the boiling point <i>T</i><sub>b</sub>, the <a href="/wiki/Entropy_of_vaporization" title="Entropy of vaporization">entropy of vaporization</a> is

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Approaches_to_understanding_entropy">Approaches to understanding entropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Approaches to understanding entropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As a fundamental aspect of thermodynamics and physics, several different approaches to entropy beyond that of Clausius and Boltzmann are valid.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Standard_textbook_definitions">Standard textbook definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Standard textbook definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following is a list of additional definitions of entropy from a collection of textbooks:
</p>
<ul><li>a measure of <a href="/wiki/Energy_dispersal" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy dispersal">energy dispersal</a> at a specific temperature.</li>
<li>a measure of disorder in the universe or of the availability of the energy in a system to do work.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>a measure of a system's <a href="/wiki/Thermal_energy" title="Thermal energy">thermal energy</a> per unit temperature that is unavailable for doing useful <a href="/wiki/Work_(thermodynamics)" title="Work (thermodynamics)">work</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>In Boltzmann's analysis in terms of constituent particles, entropy is a measure of the number of possible microscopic states (or microstates) of a system in thermodynamic equilibrium.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Order_and_disorder">Order and disorder</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Order and disorder">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Entropy_(order_and_disorder)" title="Entropy (order and disorder)">Entropy (order and disorder)</a></div>
<p>Entropy is often loosely associated with the amount of <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/order" class="extiw" title="wikt:order">order</a> or <a href="/wiki/Randomness" title="Randomness">disorder</a>, or of <a href="/wiki/Chaos_theory" title="Chaos theory">chaos</a>, in a <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_system" title="Thermodynamic system">thermodynamic system</a>. The traditional qualitative description of entropy is that it refers to changes in the status quo of the system and is a measure of "molecular disorder" and the amount of wasted energy in a dynamical energy transformation from one state or form to another. In this direction, several recent authors have derived exact entropy formulas to account for and measure disorder and order in atomic and molecular assemblies.<sup id="cite_ref-Brooks_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brooks-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Landsberg-A_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Landsberg-A-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Landsberg-B_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Landsberg-B-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> One of the simpler entropy order/disorder formulas is that derived in 1984 by thermodynamic physicist Peter Landsberg, based on a combination of <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamics" title="Thermodynamics">thermodynamics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Information_theory" title="Information theory">information theory</a> arguments. He argues that when constraints operate on a system, such that it is prevented from entering one or more of its possible or permitted states, as contrasted with its forbidden states, the measure of the total amount of "disorder" in the system is given by:<sup id="cite_ref-Landsberg-A_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Landsberg-A-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Landsberg-B_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Landsberg-B-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\text{Disorder}}={C_{\text{D}} \over C_{\text{I}}}.\,}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mtext>Disorder</mtext>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <msub>
              <mi>C</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mtext>D</mtext>
              </mrow>
            </msub>
            <msub>
              <mi>C</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mtext>I</mtext>
              </mrow>
            </msub>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\text{Disorder}}={C_{\text{D}} \over C_{\text{I}}}.\,}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b5a1c69779f9d506c6eb0c0474760291c750ccc6" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:16.767ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\text{Disorder}}={C_{\text{D}} \over C_{\text{I}}}.\,}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Similarly, the total amount of "order" in the system is given by:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\text{Order}}=1-{C_{\text{O}} \over C_{\text{I}}}.\,}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mtext>Order</mtext>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>1</mn>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <msub>
              <mi>C</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mtext>O</mtext>
              </mrow>
            </msub>
            <msub>
              <mi>C</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mtext>I</mtext>
              </mrow>
            </msub>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\text{Order}}=1-{C_{\text{O}} \over C_{\text{I}}}.\,}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6eee560267fb45e47538589cb8186f4fb3631452" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:18.1ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\text{Order}}=1-{C_{\text{O}} \over C_{\text{I}}}.\,}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>In which <i>C</i><sub>D</sub> is the "disorder" capacity of the system, which is the entropy of the parts contained in the permitted ensemble, <i>C</i><sub>I</sub> is the "information" capacity of the system, an expression similar to Shannon's <a href="/wiki/Channel_capacity" title="Channel capacity">channel capacity</a>, and <i>C</i><sub>O</sub> is the "order" capacity of the system.<sup id="cite_ref-Brooks_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brooks-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_dispersal">Energy dispersal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Energy dispersal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

In the very short time period of the breaking process, the entropy of the mass making up the glass cup rises sharply, as the matter and energy of the glass disperse.</div></div></div>
<p>The concept of entropy can be described qualitatively as a measure of energy dispersal at a specific temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Similar terms have been in use from early in the history of <a href="/wiki/Classical_thermodynamics" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical thermodynamics">classical thermodynamics</a>, and with the development of <a href="/wiki/Statistical_thermodynamics" class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical thermodynamics">statistical thermodynamics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum theory</a>, entropy changes have been described in terms of the mixing or "spreading" of the total energy of each constituent of a system over its particular quantized energy levels.
</p><p>Ambiguities in the terms <i>disorder</i> and <i>chaos</i>, which usually have meanings directly opposed to equilibrium, contribute to widespread confusion and hamper comprehension of entropy for most students.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> As the <a href="/wiki/Second_law_of_thermodynamics" title="Second law of thermodynamics">second law of thermodynamics</a> shows, in an <a href="/wiki/Isolated_system" title="Isolated system">isolated system</a> internal portions at different temperatures tend to adjust to a single uniform temperature and thus produce equilibrium. A recently developed educational approach avoids ambiguous terms and describes such spreading out of energy as dispersal, which leads to loss of the differentials required for work even though the total energy remains constant in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/First_law_of_thermodynamics" title="First law of thermodynamics">first law of thermodynamics</a><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> (compare discussion in next section). Physical chemist <a href="/wiki/Peter_Atkins" title="Peter Atkins">Peter Atkins</a>, in his textbook <i>Physical Chemistry</i>, introduces entropy with the statement that "spontaneous changes are always accompanied by a dispersal of energy or matter and often both".<sup id="cite_ref-AtkinsPaula2019_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AtkinsPaula2019-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relating_entropy_to_energy_usefulness">Relating entropy to energy <i>usefulness</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Relating entropy to energy usefulness">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is possible (in a thermal context) to regard lower entropy as a measure of the <i>effectiveness</i> or <i>usefulness</i> of a particular quantity of energy.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>  Energy supplied at a higher temperature (i.e. with low entropy) tends to be more useful than the same amount of energy available at a lower temperature. Mixing a hot parcel of a fluid with a cold one produces a parcel of intermediate temperature, in which the overall increase in entropy represents a "loss" that can never be replaced.
</p><p>As the entropy of the universe is steadily increasing, its total energy is becoming less useful. Eventually, this leads to the <a href="/wiki/Heat_death_of_the_universe" title="Heat death of the universe">heat death of the universe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entropy_and_adiabatic_accessibility">Entropy and adiabatic accessibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Entropy and adiabatic accessibility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A definition of entropy based entirely on the relation of <a href="/wiki/Adiabatic_accessibility" title="Adiabatic accessibility">adiabatic accessibility</a> between equilibrium states was given by <a href="/wiki/Elliott_H._Lieb" title="Elliott H. Lieb">E.H.Lieb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jakob_Yngvason" title="Jakob Yngvason">J. Yngvason</a> in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> This approach has several predecessors, including the pioneering work of <a href="/wiki/Constantin_Carath%C3%A9odory" title="Constantin Carathéodory">Constantin Carathéodory</a> from 1909<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and the monograph by R. Giles.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In the setting of Lieb and Yngvason one starts by picking, for a unit amount of the substance under consideration, two reference states <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X_{0}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X_{0}}</annotation>

Defining the entropies of the reference states to be 0 and 1 respectively the entropy of a state <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X}">

A simple but important result within this setting is that entropy is uniquely determined, apart from a choice of unit and an additive constant for each chemical element, by the following properties: It is monotonic with respect to the relation of adiabatic accessibility, additive on composite systems, and extensive under scaling.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entropy_in_quantum_mechanics">Entropy in quantum mechanics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Entropy in quantum mechanics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Von_Neumann_entropy" title="Von Neumann entropy">von Neumann entropy</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Quantum_statistical_mechanics" title="Quantum statistical mechanics">quantum statistical mechanics</a>, the concept of entropy was developed by <a href="/wiki/John_von_Neumann" title="John von Neumann">John von Neumann</a> and is generally referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Von_Neumann_entropy" title="Von Neumann entropy">von Neumann entropy</a>",
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S=-k_{\mathrm {B} }\operatorname {Tr} (\rho \log \rho ),}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>k</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi>
            </mrow>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>Tr</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>&#x03C1;<!-- ρ --></mi>
        <mi>log</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mi>&#x03C1;<!-- ρ --></mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S=-k_{\mathrm {B} }\operatorname {Tr} (\rho \log \rho ),}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fb926384e7517d1a0e70dcb10129d463ed0f51bd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:20.596ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle S=-k_{\mathrm {B} }\operatorname {Tr} (\rho \log \rho ),}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where <i>ρ</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Density_matrix" title="Density matrix">density matrix</a> and Tr is the <a href="/wiki/Trace_(linear_algebra)" title="Trace (linear algebra)">trace</a> operator.
</p><p>This upholds the <a href="/wiki/Correspondence_principle" title="Correspondence principle">correspondence principle</a>, because in the <a href="/wiki/Classical_limit" title="Classical limit">classical limit</a>, when the phases between the basis states used for the classical probabilities are purely random, this expression is equivalent to the familiar classical definition of entropy,
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S=-k_{\mathrm {B} }\sum _{i}p_{i}\,\log \,p_{i},}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>k</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi>
            </mrow>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <munder>
          <mo>&#x2211;<!-- ∑ --></mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </munder>
        <msub>
          <mi>p</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>log</mi>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <msub>
          <mi>p</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S=-k_{\mathrm {B} }\sum _{i}p_{i}\,\log \,p_{i},}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ae6912841d70818a0d58361844b5ea79f2aaa561" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:22.247ex; height:5.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle S=-k_{\mathrm {B} }\sum _{i}p_{i}\,\log \,p_{i},}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>i.e. in such a basis the density matrix is diagonal.
</p><p>Von Neumann established a rigorous mathematical framework for quantum mechanics with his work <i>Mathematische Grundlagen der Quantenmechanik</i>. He provided in this work a theory of measurement, where the usual notion of <a href="/wiki/Wave_function_collapse" title="Wave function collapse">wave function collapse</a> is described as an irreversible process (the so-called von Neumann or projective measurement). Using this concept, in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Density_matrix" title="Density matrix">density matrix</a> he extended the classical concept of entropy into the quantum domain.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_theory">Information theory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Information theory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Entropy_(information_theory)" title="Entropy (information theory)">Entropy (information theory)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Entropy_in_thermodynamics_and_information_theory" title="Entropy in thermodynamics and information theory">Entropy in thermodynamics and information theory</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Entropic_uncertainty" title="Entropic uncertainty">Entropic uncertainty</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1062260506"/><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:30em; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>I thought of calling it "information", but the word was overly used, so I decided to call it "uncertainty". [...] Von Neumann told me, "You should call it entropy, for two reasons. In the first place your uncertainty function has been used in statistical mechanics under that name, so it already has a name. In the second place, and more important, nobody knows what entropy really is, so in a debate you will always have the advantage."
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">Conversation between <a href="/wiki/Claude_Shannon" title="Claude Shannon">Claude Shannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_von_Neumann" title="John von Neumann">John von Neumann</a> regarding what name to give to the <a href="/wiki/Attenuation" title="Attenuation">attenuation</a> in phone-line signals<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>When viewed in terms of <a href="/wiki/Information_theory" title="Information theory">information theory</a>, the entropy state function is the amount of information in the system that is needed to fully specify the microstate of the system. Entropy is the measure of the amount of missing information before reception.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Often called <i>Shannon entropy</i>, it was originally devised by <a href="/wiki/Claude_Shannon" title="Claude Shannon">Claude Shannon</a> in 1948 to study the size of information of a transmitted message. The definition of information entropy is expressed in terms of a discrete set of probabilities <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle p_{i}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>p</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5bab39399bf5424f25d957cdc57c84a0622626d2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:2.059ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="p_{i}"/></span> so that
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle H(X)=-\sum _{i=1}^{n}p(x_{i})\log p(x_{i}).}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>H</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <munderover>
          <mo>&#x2211;<!-- ∑ --></mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
            <mo>=</mo>
            <mn>1</mn>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>n</mi>
          </mrow>
        </munderover>
        <mi>p</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mi>log</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mi>p</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle H(X)=-\sum _{i=1}^{n}p(x_{i})\log p(x_{i}).}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7de5d59a442f5305853d4392826b1f51dc43f6d0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:29.498ex; height:6.843ex;" alt="H(X)=-\sum _{i=1}^{n}p(x_{i})\log p(x_{i})."/></span></dd></dl>
<p>In the case of transmitted messages, these probabilities were the probabilities that a particular message was actually transmitted, and the entropy of the message system was a measure of the average size of information of a message. For the case of equal probabilities (i.e. each message is equally probable), the Shannon entropy (in bits) is just the number of binary questions needed to determine the content of the message.<sup id="cite_ref-Perplexed_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perplexed-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Most researchers consider information entropy and thermodynamic entropy directly linked to the same concept,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Georgescu-Roegen_1971_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgescu-Roegen_1971-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> while others argue that they are distinct.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Both expressions are mathematically similar. If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle W}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>W</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle W}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/54a9c4c547f4d6111f81946cad242b18298d70b7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.435ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="W"/></span> is the number of microstates that can yield a given macrostate, and each microstate has the same <i><a href="/wiki/A_priori_knowledge" class="mw-redirect" title="A priori knowledge">a priori</a></i> probability, then that probability is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle p=1/W}">

Some authors argue for dropping the word entropy for the <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle H}">

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Measurement">Measurement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Measurement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The entropy of a substance can be measured, although in an indirect way. The measurement, known as entropymetry,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> is done on a closed system (with particle number N and volume V being constants) and uses the definition of temperature<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> in terms of entropy, while limiting energy exchange to heat (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle dU\rightarrow dQ}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>U</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>Q</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle dU\rightarrow dQ}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c2c0b27db26c1bf25f28ab8b710b54c9c70ecb67" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:9.667ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle dU\rightarrow dQ}"/></span>).
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle T:=\left({\frac {\partial U}{\partial S}}\right)_{V,N}\Rightarrow \cdots \Rightarrow \;dS=dQ/T}">

            <mi>V</mi>

          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo stretchy="false">&#x21D2;<!-- ⇒ --></mo>

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d5e153d6b827963d81eaad5fa971d87ac2b271de" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.838ex; width:38.415ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle T:=\left({\frac {\partial U}{\partial S}}\right)_{V,N}\Rightarrow \cdots \Rightarrow \;dS=dQ/T}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>The resulting relation describes how entropy changes <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle dS}">
