    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle dS}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/66f6ab8a2a8b85df78efbea896fcfeb3d4ea39e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.715ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="dS"/></span> when a small amount of energy <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle dQ}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>d</mi>
        <mi>Q</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle dQ}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e163c727d96a2674abb2a76aae5fd803aded2304" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.054ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="dQ"/></span> is introduced into the system at a certain temperature&#160;<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle T}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>T</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle T}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec7200acd984a1d3a3d7dc455e262fbe54f7f6e0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.636ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="T"/></span>.
</p><p>The process of measurement goes as follows. First, a sample of the substance is cooled as close to absolute zero as possible. At such temperatures, the entropy approaches zero&#160;&#8211;&#32;due to the definition of temperature. Then, small amounts of heat are introduced into the sample and the change in temperature is recorded, until the temperature reaches a desired value (usually 25&#160;°C). The obtained data allows the user to integrate the equation above, yielding the absolute value of entropy of the substance at the final temperature. This value of entropy is called calorimetric entropy.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Interdisciplinary_applications">Interdisciplinary applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Interdisciplinary applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Although the concept of entropy was originally a thermodynamic concept, it has been adapted in other fields of study,<sup id="cite_ref-Pokrovskii_2020_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pokrovskii_2020-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Information_theory" title="Information theory">information theory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychodynamics" title="Psychodynamics">psychodynamics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thermoeconomics" title="Thermoeconomics">thermoeconomics</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ecological_economics" title="Ecological economics">ecological economics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brooks_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brooks-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philosophy_and_theoretical_physics">Philosophy and theoretical physics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Philosophy and theoretical physics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Entropy is the only quantity in the physical sciences that seems to imply a particular direction of progress, sometimes called an <a href="/wiki/Arrow_of_time" title="Arrow of time">arrow of time</a>. As time progresses, the second law of thermodynamics states that the entropy of an <a href="/wiki/Isolated_system" title="Isolated system">isolated system</a> never decreases in large systems over significant periods of time. Hence, from this perspective, entropy measurement is thought of as a clock in these conditions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biology">Biology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Biology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chiavazzo <i>et&#160;al.</i> proposed that where cave spiders choose to lay their eggs can be explained through entropy minimization.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Entropy has been proven useful in the analysis of base pair sequences in DNA. Many entropy-based measures have been shown to distinguish between different structural regions of the genome, differentiate between coding and non-coding regions of DNA, and can also be applied for the recreation of evolutionary trees by determining the evolutionary distance between different species.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cosmology">Cosmology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Cosmology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Assuming that a finite universe is an isolated system, the second law of thermodynamics states that its total entropy is continually increasing. It has been speculated, since the 19th century, that the universe is fated to a <a href="/wiki/Heat_death_of_the_universe" title="Heat death of the universe">heat death</a> in which all the energy ends up as a homogeneous distribution of thermal energy so that no more work can be extracted from any source.
</p><p>If the universe can be considered to have generally increasing entropy, then – as <a href="/wiki/Roger_Penrose" title="Roger Penrose">Roger Penrose</a> has pointed out – <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">gravity</a> plays an important role in the increase because gravity causes dispersed matter to accumulate into stars, which collapse eventually into <a href="/wiki/Black_hole" title="Black hole">black holes</a>. <a href="/wiki/Black_hole_entropy" class="mw-redirect" title="Black hole entropy">The entropy of a black hole</a> is proportional to the surface area of the black hole's <a href="/wiki/Event_horizon" title="Event horizon">event horizon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Bekenstein" title="Jacob Bekenstein">Jacob Bekenstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a> have shown that black holes have the maximum possible entropy of any object of equal size. This makes them likely end points of all entropy-increasing processes, if they are totally effective matter and energy traps.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> However, the escape of energy from black holes might be possible due to quantum activity (see <a href="/wiki/Hawking_radiation" title="Hawking radiation">Hawking radiation</a>).
</p><p>The role of entropy in cosmology remains a controversial subject since the time of <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Boltzmann" title="Ludwig Boltzmann">Ludwig Boltzmann</a>. Recent work has cast some doubt on the heat death hypothesis and the applicability of any simple thermodynamic model to the universe in general. Although entropy does increase in the model of an expanding universe, the maximum possible entropy rises much more rapidly, moving the universe further from the heat death with time, not closer.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> This results in an "entropy gap" pushing the system further away from the posited heat death equilibrium.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Other complicating factors, such as the energy density of the vacuum and macroscopic <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum</a> effects, are difficult to reconcile with thermodynamical models, making any predictions of large-scale thermodynamics extremely difficult.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Current theories suggest the entropy gap to have been originally opened up by <a href="/wiki/Inflation_(cosmology)" title="Inflation (cosmology)">the early rapid exponential expansion</a> of the universe.<sup id="cite_ref-Albrecht_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Albrecht-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Entropy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Georgescu-Roegen#The_relevance_of_thermodynamics_to_economics" title="Nicholas Georgescu-Roegen">Nicholas Georgescu-Roegen  §&#160;The relevance of thermodynamics to economics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ecological_economics#Methodology" title="Ecological economics">Ecological economics  §&#160;Methodology</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Romanian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian American">Romanian American</a> economist <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Georgescu-Roegen" title="Nicholas Georgescu-Roegen">Nicholas Georgescu-Roegen</a>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_considered_father_or_mother_of_a_scientific_field" title="List of people considered father or mother of a scientific field">progenitor</a> in economics and a <a href="/wiki/Paradigm_shift#Kuhnian_paradigm_shifts" title="Paradigm shift">paradigm founder</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ecological_economics" title="Ecological economics">ecological economics</a>, made extensive use of the entropy concept in his <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Georgescu-Roegen#Magnum_opus_on_The_Entropy_Law_and_the_Economic_Process" title="Nicholas Georgescu-Roegen">magnum opus on <i>The Entropy Law and the Economic Process</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Georgescu-Roegen_1971_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgescu-Roegen_1971-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Due to Georgescu-Roegen's work, the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_thermodynamics" title="Laws of thermodynamics">laws of thermodynamics</a> form an <a href="/wiki/Ecological_economics#Methodology" title="Ecological economics">integral part of the ecological economics school</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 204f">&#58;&#8202;204f&#8202;</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 29–35">&#58;&#8202;29–35&#8202;</span></sup> Although his work was <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Georgescu-Roegen#Mistakes_and_controversies" title="Nicholas Georgescu-Roegen">blemished somewhat by mistakes</a>, a full chapter on the economics of Georgescu-Roegen has approvingly been included in one elementary physics textbook on the historical development of thermodynamics.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 95–112">&#58;&#8202;95–112&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>In economics, Georgescu-Roegen's work has generated the term <a href="/wiki/Pessimism#Entropy_pessimism" title="Pessimism">'entropy pessimism'</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 116">&#58;&#8202;116&#8202;</span></sup> Since the 1990s, leading ecological economist and <a href="/wiki/Steady-state_economy#Herman_Daly&#39;s_concept_of_a_steady-state_economy" title="Steady-state economy">steady-state theorist</a> <a href="/wiki/Herman_Daly" title="Herman Daly">Herman Daly</a> – a student of Georgescu-Roegen – has been the economics profession's most influential proponent of the entropy pessimism position.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 545f">&#58;&#8202;545f&#8202;</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

A Greek–English Lexicon, revised and augmented edition, Oxford University Press, Oxford UK, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974"/><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0198642148" title="Special:BookSources/0198642148">0198642148</a>, pp. 1826–1827.</span>

<li id="cite_note-Clausius_German-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Clausius_German_9-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Clausius_German_9-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974"/><cite id="CITEREFClausius1865" class="citation journal cs1">Clausius, Rudolf (1865). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://zenodo.org/record/1423700">"Ueber verschiedene für die Anwendung bequeme Formen der Hauptgleichungen der mechanischen Wärmetheorie (Vorgetragen in der naturforsch. Gesellschaft zu Zürich den 24. April 1865)"</a>. <i>Annalen der Physik und Chemie</i>. <b>125</b> (7): 353–400. <a href="/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bibcode (identifier)">Bibcode</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1865AnP...201..353C">1865AnP...201..353C</a>. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1002%2Fandp.18652010702">10.1002/andp.18652010702</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Annalen+der+Physik+und+Chemie&amp;rft.atitle=Ueber+verschiedene+f%C3%BCr+die+Anwendung+bequeme+Formen+der+Hauptgleichungen+der+mechanischen+W%C3%A4rmetheorie+%28Vorgetragen+in+der+naturforsch.+Gesellschaft+zu+Z%C3%BCrich+den+24.+April+1865%29&amp;rft.volume=125&amp;rft.issue=7&amp;rft.pages=353-400&amp;rft.date=1865&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1002%2Fandp.18652010702&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F1865AnP...201..353C&amp;rft.aulast=Clausius&amp;rft.aufirst=Rudolf&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fzenodo.org%2Frecord%2F1423700&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEntropy" class="Z3988"></span> "Sucht man für <i>S</i> einen bezeichnenden Namen, so könnte man, ähnlich wie von der Gröſse <i>U</i> gesagt ist, sie sey der <i>Wärme- und Werkinhalt</i> des Körpers, von der Gröſse <i>S</i> sagen, sie sey der <i>Verwandlungsinhalt</i> des Körpers. Da ich es aber für besser halte, die Namen derartiger für die Wissenschaft wichtiger Gröſsen aus den alten Sprachen zu entnehmen, damit sie unverändert in allen neuen Sprachen angewandt werden können, so schlage ich vor, die Gröſse <i>S</i> nach dem griechischen Worte ἡ τροπή, die Verwandlung, die <i>Entropie</i> des Körpers zu nennen. Das Wort <i>Entropie</i> habei ich absichtlich dem Worte <i>Energie</i> möglichst ähnlich gebildet, denn die beiden Gröſsen, welche durch diese Worte benannt werden sollen, sind ihren physikalischen Bedeutungen nach einander so nahe verwandt, daſs eine gewisse Gleichartigkeit in der Benennung mir zweckmäſsig zu seyn scheint." (p. 390).</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Gil399-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Gil399_10-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Gil399_10-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974"/><cite id="CITEREFGillispie1960" class="citation book cs1"><a href="/wiki/Charles_Coulston_Gillispie" title="Charles Coulston Gillispie">Gillispie, Charles Coulston</a> (1960). <span class="cs1-lock-registration" title="Free registration required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/edgeofobjectivit0000gill"><i>The Edge of Objectivity: An Essay in the History of Scientific Ideas</i></a></span>. Princeton University Press. p.&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/edgeofobjectivit0000gill/page/399">399</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-691-02350-6" title="Special:BookSources/0-691-02350-6"><bdi>0-691-02350-6</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Edge+of+Objectivity%3A+An+Essay+in+the+History+of+Scientific+Ideas&amp;rft.pages=399&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1960&amp;rft.isbn=0-691-02350-6&amp;rft.aulast=Gillispie&amp;rft.aufirst=Charles+Coulston&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Fedgeofobjectivit0000gill&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEntropy" class="Z3988"></span> "Clausius coined the word entropy for <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>

    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span>: ″I prefer going to the ancient languages for the names of important scientific quantities, so that they may mean the same thing in all living tongues. I propose, accordingly, to call <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S}">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span> the entropy of a body, after the Greek word 'transformation.' I have designedly coined the word entropy to be similar to 'energy,' for these two quantities are so analogous in their physical significance, that an analogy of denomination seemed to me helpful.″"</span>
